## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|

| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Platform Engineering: CODEOWNERS Infrastructure Discovery

## Your Task

Your platform team needs to understand how code ownership works in Grafana — not just the CODEOWNERS file itself, but the entire infrastructure around it: manifest generation, CI validation, Go integration with feature management, and npm scripts.

**Specific question**: Find all files in `grafana/grafana` that form the CODEOWNERS infrastructure:

1. **The actual CODEOWNERS file** — the GitHub ownership definition
2. **CI workflows** that validate CODEOWNERS
3. **Manifest generation scripts** (JavaScript) that parse and index CODEOWNERS
4. **Go code** that defines the `codeowner` type for feature management
5. **npm scripts** that orchestrate manifest generation

This crosses YAML (CI), JavaScript (scripts), Go (backend), and file ownership conventions.

## Context

You are a platform engineer investigating how code ownership is implemented and enforced in a large monorepo. Understanding this infrastructure is critical for onboarding new teams, debugging CI failures related to CODEOWNERS validation, and extending the ownership system to new areas of the codebase.

## Available Resources

Your ecosystem includes the following repositories:
- `grafana/grafana` at v11.4.0

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "grafana/grafana", "path": "relative/path/to/file"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of the CODEOWNERS infrastructure."
}
```

**Important**: Use `"grafana/grafana"` for the repo name. Strip `github.com/` prefix.
**Note**: Sourcegraph MCP tools return repo names with a `github.com/` prefix (e.g., `github.com/grafana/grafana`). Strip this prefix in your answer.

Include only the `files` field. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all files that form the CODEOWNERS infrastructure?
- **Keyword presence**: Does your answer reference key identifiers (CODEOWNERS, codeowners-manifest, codeowner)?

1. **GitHub Integration**: `.github/CODEOWNERS` - the source of truth for file ownership

8. **Generated Manifests**: `pkg/services/featuremgmt/toggles_gen.json` and `toggles_gen.csv` - structured data exports

### Kubernetes API Layer:
9. **Feature Toggle Types**: `pkg/apis/featuretoggle/v0alpha1/types.go` - Feature resource definitions with codeowner field

11. **NPM Dependencies**: `package.json` - declares the codeowners package and orchestration scripts

This file is automatically validated by the `.github/workflows/codeowners-validator.yml` CI workflow using the mszostok/codeowners-validator action, which checks syntax, prevents duplicate patterns, and ensures all files have designated owners.\\n\\nIn the Go backend, code ownership is formalized through the feature management system. The `pkg/services/featuremgmt/codeowners.go` file defines a `codeowner` type and declares constants for team references (e.g., `@grafana/grafana-app-platform-squad`). These references must match the format used in the CODEOWNERS file. The `pkg/services/featuremgmt/models.go` file defines the `FeatureFlag` struct with an `Owner` field of type `codeowner`, associating each feature toggle with a responsible team.\\n\\nFeature flag definitions are centralized in `pkg/services/featuremgmt/registry.go`, where each flag specifies an owner, description, stage (experimental/preview/GA/deprecated), and other metadata. The `pkg/services/featuremgmt/toggles_gen_test.go` test file orchestrates the generation of multiple output files from this registry. When tests run, they generate: (1) `toggles_gen.go` - Go constants for all feature flags; (2) `toggles_gen.json` - a Kubernetes-style manifest containing feature metadata including the codeowner field; (3) `toggles_gen.csv` - a CSV export of feature metadata; (4) TypeScript type definitions in `packages/grafana-data/src/types/featureToggles.gen.ts`; and (5) documentation in `docs/sources/setup-grafana/configure-grafana/feature-toggles/index.md`.\\n\\nThe Kubernetes feature toggle API layer is defined in `pkg/apis/featuretoggle/v0alpha1/types.go`, which declares the Feature, FeatureList, and FeatureToggles resource types with an `Owner` (mapped to JSON as `codeowner`) field in the FeatureSpec.\\n\\nOn the npm side, the JavaScript infrastructure includes the `codeowners` npm package (version ^5.1.1, declared in `package.json`) which parses the CODEOWNERS file and provides owner lookup functionality. The `scripts/cli/generateBettererIssues.ts` script uses this package to parse CODEOWNERS and route code quality issues to the responsible team owners based on file ownership patterns.\\n\\nThe `package.json` file defines the `betterer:issues` npm script that executes the generateBettererIssues TypeScript tool, orchestrating manifest generation and issue assignment workflows. The `Makefile` provides the `gen-feature-toggles` target that runs the Go test twice to ensure feature flags are properly generated and validated.\\n\\nDocumentation in `contribute/feature-toggles.md` explains how to define new features and directs developers to update the CODEOWNERS file and use the registry-based codeowner system for feature ownership declaration.\\n\\nThis infrastructure ensures that code ownership is consistently enforced across multiple layers: GitHub's native CODEOWNERS validation, Go's type-safe feature management with codeowner integration, Kubernetes API resource definitions, and npm-based tools for parsing ownership information and routing quality issues to the appropriate teams.\"\n}\n",
